mute\r\nNH - Natural Harmonic\r\nB  - Bend (I\\\'ve placed how much to bend over the measure; for example a\r\n     .25 is a quarter step bend, a .5 is a half step bend, a .75 is a\r\n      three fourths step bend, a 1 would be a whole step bend, 2.5 would\r\n      be a two and a half step bend, etc.\r\nPb - Pre-Bend: The note is bent to a pre-determined pitch before it is\r\n      picked.\r\n\r\nPbr- Pre-Bend Release: The note is bent to a predetermined pitch before it\r\nis picked and is released to its original pitch.\r\n\r\nBrh- Bend Release Hammer-on: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its\r\n      Original pitch then either hammer-on or pull-off to a higher or\r\n      Lower fret.\r\n\r\n/  - Slide: If I have to explain this one you shouldn\\\'t be playing this\r\n        song.\r\n\r\nH  - Hammer-on\r\n\r\nBr - Bend-Release: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its original\r\n      Pitch.\r\n\r\n~~ - Vibrato: Vibrating a string either by moving up and down with your\r\n      fingers or by using a whammy bar.\r\n\r\n^  - Roll\r\n\r\nP.S. - Pitch Shifter: Use a pitch shifter when this is notated.\r\n\r\nT.P. - Tremolo Pick: Tremolo pick (play notes really fast) when this is notated.\r\n\r\n    - Fade out: Note is faded out with volume knob, volume pedal, or with an E-bow.\r\n\r\nGuitar 1: Acoustic (Thom/ Doubled by gtr.4 throughout the bottom of the tab. \r\n\r\nUpdate: January 21, 2004: After hours of looking at live concert \r\nfootage of the band and looking at what each person in the band \r\nis playing I will correct all the mistakes in this tab and make \r\ndamn near as perfect as is possible. I will do this in a wierd \r\nway though. Rather than altering the presently posted tab (which\r\nin my opinion sounds great) I will add the changes at the end \r\nof the transcription in an update section, I do this to give \r\nyou a choice because some of the corrections are more difficult\r\nto play. Most of the corrections involve the chords Thom plays\r\nduring  the "ambition make you pretty ugly" and "rain down" \r\nsections. The chords in this tab are the correct chords, \r\nThom just plays them in a different position on the fretboard. \r\nOh and if you have any comments or corrections please post them. \r\nAnd please vote for this tab if you can.\r\n  \r\n\r\nPerformance Notes:\r\n\r\nOk lets begin with Guitar 1 which is Thom Yorke. This\r\npart was played with a pick and it is quite complex looking \r\nbecause of the loose picking pattern. It is best not to try \r\nto hit every note exactly, just try to get the vibe of the \r\nsong. Any part that guitar 1 repeats is played similarly on repeats.\r\n\r\nGuitar 2 is Jonny Greenwood, his insane playing style is so \r\ndistinctive it is impossible for it to be anyone else. \r\nFor this part you\'re going to need a delay pedal, flanger, \r\nand a pitch shifter. Johnny plays some crazy harmonics like \r\n2.5 which is halfway between the second and third fret. I \r\nsuggest you read the attached legend in order to decipher \r\nthe method I used to arrange his bends and pre-bends.\r\n\r\nOne last note about guitar 3 (Ed O\' Brien), if you do not \r\nown a guitar with 24 frets don\'t worry you can tune up \r\nyour high e and b strings a whole step and just play the\r\npart relative to your new tuning. Or if you have and \r\noctave effects pedal you can just set it to raise the \r\npitch of the guitar one octave and play the part at the tenth fret.\r\n\r\n\r\nLegend:\r\n\r\n(5)- Ghost Note: A note in parenthesis that is barely heard in a recording\r\nor represents a note that is supposed to ring for longer than one measure. \r\nPM - Palm mute\r\nNH - Natural Harmonic\r\nB  - Bend (I\'ve placed how much to bend over the measure; for example a      \r\n     .25 is a quarter step bend, a .5 is a half step bend, a .75 is a \r\n      three fourths step bend, a 1 would be a whole step bend, 2.5 would   \r\n      be a two and a half step bend, etc.\r\nPb - Pre-Bend: The note is bent to a pre-determined pitch before it is  \r\n      picked.\r\n\r\nPbr- Pre-Bend Release: The note is bent to a predetermined pitch before it \r\nis picked and is released to its original pitch. \r\n\r\nBrh- Bend Release Hammer-on: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its \r\n      Original pitch then either hammer-on or pull-off to a higher or \r\n      Lower fret.\r\n\r\n/  - Slide: If I have to explain this one you shouldn\'t be playing this \r\n \tsong.\r\n\r\nH  - Hammer-on     \r\n\r\nBr - Bend-Release: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its original\r\n      Pitch.\r\n~~ - Vibrato: Vibrating a string either by moving up and down with your\r\n      fingers or by using a whammy bar.\r\n\r\n\r\nWell Anyways here you go. Radiohead\r\n-------------------------------------------------------------------------------\r\nTabbed by: Jon Stradinger\r\nEmail: heylookasensai@yahoo.com\r\n\r\nIt is my firm belief that this song, originally called "open pick", was called\r\nthis because the tuning allows for an almost open picking scheme in the key of D - \r\nyou can pick pretty much any string that you want and it will fit into the song which\r\nadds to its many intricacies. It is also my firm belief that someone needs\r\nto REALLY tab this song. This is the acoustic guitar part - hopefully I will add\r\nthe electric guitar parts later. Enjoi.\r\n\r\nthis tab is seperated into 4/4 bars when counting very fast - around 155 bpm.\r\nAlso, the point of the song is to throw your hands around a bit to get other nuances \r\nin there - this is a rough outline, but the sequence of the notes should give the\r\ngist of the song. I prefer to finger pick but whatevaz.\r\n\r\nTuning:DADGBd\r\n\r\nINTRO:\r\n\r\nd|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nB|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nG|-----7-----7---7-|-----7-----7---7-|-----7-----7---7-|-----7-----7---7-|\r\nD|---9-----9-----9-|---9-----9-----9-|---9-----9-9---9-|---9-----9-9---9-|\r\nA|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nD|-9-----9-----9---|-9-----9-----9---|-9-----9-----9---|-9-----9-----9---|\r\n\r\nd|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nB|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nG|\\----6-----6---6-|-----6-----6---6-|-----6-----6---6-|---4---4---------|\r\nD|\\--8-----8-----8-|---8-----8-----8-|---4-----4-----4-|---4---4---------|\r\nA|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|\r\nD|\\8-----8-----8---|-8-----8-----8---|-0-----0-----0---|-0---0---------4/|\r\n\r\nd|--------------|--------------|--------------|--------------|\r\nB|--------------|--------------|--------------|--------------|\r\nG|----------4---|---6---6--/7--|----------4---|---6---6--/7--|\r\nD|----4---4-4---|---4---4---4--|----4---4-4---|---4---4---4--|\r\nA|--5-5---------|--------------|--5-5---------|--------------|\r\nD|5-----5-----5-|-4---4---4---4|5-----5-----5-|-4---4---4----|\r\n\r\nINTRO note\r\n==============================================================================='], ['I have yet to see a good tab of "The Bends" so I once again scoured the Internet\r\nto find bits and pieces that were 100% correct, or at least sound like it. What\r\nfollows is a combination of a Guitar pro file (which is pretty expensive software\r\nnot many people have), several tabs, and some tabbing by me for some spots to make\r\nit sound as close to complete as possible. I do not take credit for this transcription,\r\nI only arranged for text format and filed in spots that were empty and corrected parts\r\nthat were wrong. I do this only to help other Radiohead fans have tabs that they are\r\nconfident in being correct. I hope to do this for as many songs as I can before I get\r\ntired of this or explode, whichever comes first. If you have any requests for what\r\nsongs you want me to search for and arrange, please email me at mousey84@hotmail.com.\r\nEnjoy.\r\n\r\nAnd please Rate this tab, this took forever to arrange, you could at least take\r\na second to rate it so others can know it is good.\r\n\r\n\r\nLegend:\r\n\r\n(5)- Ghost Note: A note in parenthesis that is barely heard in a recording\r\nor represents a note that is supposed to ring for longer than one measure. \r\nPM - Palm mute\r\nNH - Natural Harmonic\r\nPH - Pinch Harmonic\r\nB  - Bend (I\'ve placed how much to bend over the measure; for example a      \r\n     .25 is a quarter step bend, a .5 is a half step bend, a .75 is a \r\n      three fourths step bend, a 1 would be a whole step bend, 2.5 would   \r\n      be a two and a half step bend, etc.\r\nPb - Pre-Bend: The note is bent to a pre-determined pitch before it is  \r\n      picked.\r\n\r\nPbr- Pre-Bend Release: The note is bent to a predetermined pitch before it \r\nis picked and is released to its original pitch. \r\n\r\nBrh- Bend Release Hammer-on: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its \r\n      Original pitch then either hammer-on or pull-off to a higher or \r\n      Lower fret.\r\n\r\n/  - Slide: If I have to explain this one you shouldn\'t be playing this \r\n        song.\r\n\r\nH  - Hammer-on     \r\n\r\nBr - Bend-Release: Bend note to a pitch then release it to its original\r\n      Pitch.\r\n~~ - Vibrato: Vibrating a string either by moving up and down with your\r\n      fingers or by using a whammy bar.\r\n\r\n\r\nNote: There\'s a third guitar in this song (Ed O\' Brien) but he tends to mostly\r\ndouble Gtr. 1 loosely so it just got cut out for the sake of making this tab\r\neasier to understand. If you\'re not familiar with this effects pedal what it does\r\nis raise or lower the pitch of the notes in increments of one or two octaves. The Pedal is\r\nessential in performing Jonny\'s parts faithfully. Many transcriptions of this song (including\r\nthe "official" tab book) have erroneously notated Jonny\'s high pitched leads in this song as\r\nbeing played high on the fretboard with a slide, I confirmed this by watching a live video of\r\nthem playing the song. Along with Whammy pedal, Jonny uses either his DOD envelope filter or\r\nhis phase shifter to achieve the weird bubbly sound that rounds off his tone.\r\n\r\n  Gtr. 1 Gagging Order\r\n\r\nTabbed by Luke Wilde and Mr. Brown\r\n\r\nWas supprised there were no fitting tabs for this song out there. So I've been busting \r\nfor the last few hours trying to figure it out. Also this is the 1st tab I've done, so \r\nformat might be weird for you. Dunno how Thom came up with this number, the tuning is well strange.\r\n\r\nFirst you have to tune your guitar up to:\r\n\r\ne\r\nC#\r\nA\r\nD\r\nA\r\nD\r\n\r\nTo get that tuning you have to tune the B and G strings up 2 notes and the low E down 2:\r\n\r\nTune the B to the 6th on the G\r\nThen the G to the 7th on the D\r\n\r\n(I cringed when I was doing this, had no clue if the strings could take the strain, but \r\nthey can, so its all good.)\r\n\r\nTo tune drop D, easiest way is to play harmonics on the 7th on the E then on the 12th on \r\nA, then get the ringing to stop.\r\n\r\nThen slap on a capo at the 1st fret and your ready.\r\n\r\n(all notes relative to capo)\r\n\r\nOh and one more thing.
